## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time through nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and external driving. The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with additional nonlinear terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping, drag-like)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear driven damped)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Coupled nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v + c3 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Morse-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) * (1 - exp(c1 * x)) (asymmetric potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power terms in x (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in oscillation
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)·v → self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Cubic position term x³ with opposite sign to linear term → double-well potential / bistability
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Products x^n · v → position-dependent damping or energy-dependent dissipation
- sin(c·x) as restoring force → bounded potential (pendulum-like) with multiple equilibria
- Odd powers of velocity (v³) → nonlinear dissipation that grows rapidly at high speeds
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase-space analysis applies
- Multiple timescales in driving terms (sum of sinusoids) → quasiperiodic or chaotic behavior

Key features: The GT contains `x*|v|^(1/3)` and `log(|v| + 1)` terms. These are non-standard terms that candidates need to reproduce.

**Critical terms to match:**
1. `log(|v| + 1)` - requires a log term
2. `x*|v|^(1/3)` - requires an x times fractional power of |v|

Let me check candidates with log terms: **24, 29, 34, 38, 46, 47**

These have `c3*log(c4*exp(c5*v) + 1)`. Note: `log(c4*exp(c5*v) + 1)` with c4=1, c5=0 gives `log(2)` (constant), not `log(|v|+1)`. This form cannot produce `log(|v|+1)` since `|v|` isn't `exp(cv)` for any constant c.

Now check candidates with `exp(c*sin(c*v + c))` terms. For small arguments, `exp(ε*sin(v))` ≈ `1 + ε*sin(v)`, but `sin(v)` is not `log(|v|+1)` or `|v|^(1/3)`.

None of the `exp(sin(...))` terms can produce `log(|v|+1)` or `|v|^(1/3)*x`.

The GT has two problematic terms: `log(|v|+1)` and `x*|v|^(1/3)`. No candidate has both. In fact, no candidate has `|v|^(1/3)*x` in any form.

The candidates with `exp(sin(...))` can't match `log(|v|+1)` — these are fundamentally different functions.

The candidates with `log(c*exp(cv)+1)` can't match `log(|v|+1)` because `exp(cv)` cannot equal `|v|` for all v.

Even if we could somehow approximate one nonlinear term, we'd still need `x*|v|^(1/3)` which appears in none of the candidates.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
-0.0441723*v³ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v²) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)
```

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x - 3.58221*0.047928*x*|v|^(1/3)`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v³ terms**: (-0.0441723 + 0.333481)*v³ = 0.289309*v³
- **v terms**: (-0.333481 - 1.24947)*v = -1.58295*v
- **x terms**: -3.58221*x
- **x*|v|^(1/3) terms**: -0.17172*x*|v|^(1/3)
- **log(|v|+1) terms**: -0.624737*log(|v| + 1)

So GT = c_a*x + c_b*v + c_c*v³ + c_d*x*|v|^(1/3) + c_e*log(|v| + 1)

The key basis functions are: **x, v, v³, x·|v|^(1/3), log(|v|+1)**

This is critical: the GT contains `x·|v|^(1/3)` and `log(|v|+1)` as essential nonlinear terms. No candidate can match unless it can reproduce these.

## Candidate Analysis

Let me check each candidate for the required basis functions: `x·|v|^(1/3)` and `log(|v|+1)`.

**Candidates with exp(sin(...))**: Candidates 1, 4-13, 16-17, 20, 28, 31-32, 41-42, 50. The function `exp(c4*sin(c5*v + c6))` cannot exactly equal `log(|v|+1)` or `x·|v|^(1/3)` for all v. These are fundamentally different basis functions. None of these can match.

**Candidates with v*sin(t+...) or v*x*cos(t)**: Candidates 2-3, 11, 14-15, 18-19, 21-23, 25-27, 29-30, 33-40, 43-49. These contain time-dependent terms. We can set their coefficients to 0, but then we're left with polynomials in x and v (plus possibly |v| terms). Polynomials cannot reproduce `log(|v|+1)` or `x·|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates with log(c4*exp(c5*v)+1)**: Candidates 24, 29, 34, 38, 46, 47.

For `log(c4*exp(c5*v)+1)`: When c4=1, c5→0, this approaches log(2), a constant. This is NOT `log(|v|+1)` since `log(|v|+1)` is symmetric in v while `log(c4*exp(c5*v)+1)` is not symmetric for any nonzero c5. And with c5=0, it's just a constant. So `log(c4*exp(c5*v)+1)` cannot reproduce `log(|v|+1)`.

Also, none of these candidates have `x·|v|^(1/3)`.

**Candidates 9, 25, 48**: These have duplicate v terms (c1*v + c9*v) which just combine. Still polynomial-based, can't match.

After thorough analysis, **no candidate** contains both `log(|v|+1)` (symmetric log) and `x·|v|^(1/3)` terms. The GT fundamentally requires these non-polynomial, non-exponential basis functions that are absent from all candidates.
